`Selector` class is the heart of Kafka's NIO-based network layer, implementing the `Selectable` interface. It manages non-blocking, multi-connection network I/O using Java's `java.nio.channels.Selector`. The Selector handles connection establishment, data transmission, and channel lifecycle management.\\n\\n### Server-Side Network Threading (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)\\n\\n**Acceptor Thread**: The abstract `Acceptor` class (lines 474-487) runs as a separate thread that accepts new socket connections and configures them with appropriate security protocols. `DataPlaneAcceptor` (lines 376-401) extends Acceptor and implements the data plane listener for broker-to-client communication. The Acceptor maintains a list of `Processor` instances and round-robins new connections to them.\\n\\n**Processor Threads**: The `Processor` class (lines 816-836) runs as a separate thread pool where each Processor:\\n- Manages a local `Selector` instance for handling NIO operations\\n- Maintains new connections via `newConnections` queue (line 844)\\n- Queues responses in `responseQueue` (line 846)\\n- Handles authentication and channel preparation\\n- Routes completed receives to the `RequestChannel`\\n\\n### Request Channel (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)\\nThe `RequestChannel` class (lines 344-351) provides the critical handoff mechanism between Processor threads and request handler threads. It:\\n- Acts as a bridge for passing requests from network I/O threads to handler threads\\n- Maintains separate queues for requests and responses\\n- Coordinates metrics collection via `RequestChannelMetrics` (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/network/metrics/RequestChannelMetrics.java)\\n\\n### Network Byte Buffer Management\\n\\n**NetworkReceive** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkReceive.java, lines 32-38):\\nImplements the `Receive` interface and manages incoming network data. Features include:\\n- Size-delimited message handling with a 4-byte size prefix\\n- Support for unlimited or bounded buffer sizes\\n- Integration with `MemoryPool` for efficient buffer allocation\\n- Automatic payload buffering and completion detection\\n\\n**NetworkSend** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkSend.java, lines 20-27):\\nWraps the `Send` interface and represents outgoing network data. Framework\\n\\n**ChannelBuilder Interface** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilder.java, lines 26-42):\\nFactory interface for creating channels with specific security (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SslChannelBuilder.java, lines 42-56): Builds SSL-encrypted channels with certificate management\\n- **SaslChannelBuilder** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java, lines 79-106): Builds SASL-authenticated channels for Kerberos/PLAIN/OAuth\\n\\n### Supporting (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/memory/MemoryPool.java, lines 26-38):\\nManages efficient buffer allocation and reuse to prevent garbage collection pressure in the network layer.\\n\\n**Selectable Interface** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selectable.java, lines 31-88):\\nAbstracts the network I/O selection API, allowing multiple implementations of the selector pattern.\\n\\n## Data Flow\\n\\n1. **Acceptor** accepts new connections and distributes them to **Processor** instances\\n2. **Processor** uses **Selector** to perform NIO operations on **KafkaChannel** instances\\n3. **NetworkReceive** buffers incoming client requests via the channel's **TransportLayer**\\n4. **RequestChannel** delivers complete requests from **Processor** to handler thread pool\\n5. **Processor** sends responses via **NetworkSend** buffers back through the network\\n6. **MemoryPool** manages buffer lifecycle to ensure efficient resource usage\\n\\nAll
